      "keystrokes": "cat > /app/steal.py << 'PYEOF'\nimport numpy as np\nfrom forward import forward\n\ndef numerical_gradient(f, x, eps=1e-5):\n    \"\"\"Numerical gradient of f at x.\"\"\"\n    grad = np.zeros_like(x)\n    for i in range(len(x)):\n        x_plus = x.copy()\n        x_plus[i] += eps\n        x_minus = x.copy()\n        x_minus[i] -= eps\n        grad[i] = (f(x_plus) - f(x_minus)) / (2 * eps)\n    return grad\n\ndef find_breakpoints(v, num_samples=1000, range_min=-5, range_max=5):\n    \"\"\"Find breakpoints along direction v by scanning f(t*v).\n    Returns a list of t values where derivative changes.\"\"\"\n    ts = np.linspace(range_min, range_max, num_samples)\n    vals = np.array([forward(t * v) for t in ts])\n    \n    # Numerical first derivative\n    h = ts[1] - ts[0]\n    derivs = (vals[1:] - vals[:-1]) / h\n    \n    # Second derivative (change in first derivative)\n    second_derivs = np.abs(np.diff(derivs))\n    \n    # Find peaks in second derivative\n    threshold = 5e-6\n    candidates = np.where(second_derivs > threshold)[0]\n    \n    # Merge nearby candidates (same breakpoint)\n    if len(candidates) == 0:\n        return []\n    \n    breakpoints = []\n    current_group = [candidates[0]]\n    for i in range(1, len(candidates)):\n        if candidates[i] - candidates[i-1] <= 2:\n            current_group.append(candidates[i])\n        else:\n            # We need to find where the derivative changes\n    # First identify which side is which\n    eps = 1e-4\n    t_left = t_approx - eps\n    t_right = t_approx + eps\n    \n    # Check if there's a sign change in the pre-activation of some neuron\n    # We can detect this by looking at the gradient change\n    \n    # Binary search for more precise location\n    lo = t_approx - 0.01\n    hi = t_approx + 0.01\n    \n    # Evaluate gradient at lo and hi\n    def f(t):\n        return forward(t * v)\n    \n    # Find a more precise breakpoint by looking for where the function behavior changes\n    # We'll use the fact that the derivative changes at the breakpoint\n    \n    grad_lo = numerical_gradient(lambda x: forward(x), lo * v)\n    grad_hi = numerical_gradient(lambda x: forward(x), hi * v)\n    \n    # The gradient difference vector (normalized) is what we want\n    diff = grad_hi - grad_lo\n    \n    # Binary search to find the exact t where diff occurs\n    for _ in range(30):\n        mid = (lo + hi) / 2\n        grad_mid_lo = numerical_gradient(lambda x: forward(x), (mid - 1e-5) * v)\n        grad_mid_hi = numerical_gradient(lambda x: forward(x), (mid + 1e-5) * v)\n        mid_diff = grad_mid_hi - grad_mid_lo\n        if np.linalg.norm(mid_diff) > np.linalg.norm(diff) * 0.5:\n            hi = mid\n        else:\n            lo = mid\n    \n    refined_t = (lo + hi) / 2\n    \n    # Compute the gradient jump at the refined point\n    g_minus = numerical_gradient(lambda x: forward(x), (refined_t - 1e-5) * v)\n    g_plus = numerical_gradient(lambda x: forward(x), (refined_t + 1e-5) * v)\n    jump = g_plus - g_minus\n    \n    return refined_t, jump, g_minus, g_plus\n\ndef extract_vectors(num_directions=200, samples_per_dir=500):\n    \"\"\"Extract gradient jump vectors from breakpoints.\"\"\"\n    all_vectors = []\n    \n    for _ in range(num_directions):\n        # Random direction\n        v = np.random.randn(10)\n        v = v / np.linalg.norm(v)\n        \n        # Find breakpoints\n        bps = find_breakpoints(v, num_samples=samples_per_dir)\n        \n        for bp in bps:\n            # Refine and get gradient jump\n            try:\n                t_refined, jump, _, _ = refine_breakpoint(v, bp)\n                # Normalize the jump vector (sign doesn't matter, we just need direction)\n                if np.linalg.norm(jump) > 1e-8:\n                    # Normalize vectors\n    norms = np.linalg.norm(vectors, axis=1, keepdims=True)\n    norms[norms == 0] = 1\n    vectors_normalized = vectors / norms\n    \n    # Also store signs: we can flip sign of vectors since scaling ambiguity\n    # For k-means we need direction, not orientation\n    \n    # Initialize with random vectors\n    n = len(vectors)\n    indices = np.random.choice(n, n_clusters, replace=False)\n    centroids = vectors_normalized[indices].copy()\n    \n    for iteration in range(n_iter):\n        # Assign each point to nearest centroid (by cosine similarity)\n        # We need to handle sign: distance = min(|c - v|, |c + v|)\n        assignments = []\n        for v in vectors_normalized:\n            # Compute distances to all centroids\n            dists_pos = np.linalg.norm(centroids - v.reshape(1, -1), axis=1)\n            dists_neg = np.linalg.norm(centroids + v.reshape(1, -1), axis=1)\n            dists = np.minimum(dists_pos, dists_neg)\n            assignments.append(np.argmin(dists))\n        assignments = np.array(assignments)\n        \n        # Update centroids\n        new_centroids = []\n        for k in range(n_clusters):\n            mask = assignments == k\n            if np.sum(mask) > 0:\n                cluster_vecs = vectors_normalized[mask]\n                # Handle sign: align all to first vector\n                ref = cluster_vecs[0]\n                aligned = []\n                for v in cluster_vecs:\n                    if np.dot(v, ref) >= 0:\n                        aligned.append(v)\n                    else:\n                        aligned.append(-v)\n                centroid = np.mean(aligned, axis=0)\n                centroid = centroid / (np.linalg.norm(centroid) + 1e-10)\n                new_centroids.append(centroid)\n            else:\n                # Random reinit\n                new_centroids.append(vectors_normalized[np.random.randint(n)])\n        centroids = np.array(new_centroids)\n        \n        # Check convergence\n        if iteration > 10 and iteration % 10 == 0:\n            pass\n    \n    return centroids\n\ndef main():\n    print(\"Extracting gradient jump vectors...\")\n    vectors = extract_vectors(num_directions=300, samples_per_dir=400)\n    print(f\"Collected {len(vectors)} vectors\")\n    \n    if len(vectors) < 20:\n        print(\"Not enough vectors found, trying more directions...\")\n        more_vectors = extract_vectors(num_directions=200, samples_per_dir=600)\n        vectors = np.vstack([vectors, more_vectors])\n        print(f\"Now have {len(vectors)} vectors\")\n    \n    np.save('/app/stolen_vectors.npy', vectors)\n    \n    print(\"Clustering vectors...\")\n    # Compute inertia\n            inertia = 0\n            for v in vectors:\n                dists = np.minimum(\n                    np.linalg.norm(centroids - v.reshape(1, -1), axis=1),\n                    np.linalg.norm(centroids + v.reshape(1, -1), axis=1)\n                )\n                inertia += np.min(dists)**2\n            if inertia < best_inertia:\n                best_inertia = inertia\n                best_centroids = centroids\n                print(f\"  Restart {restart}: inertia = {inertia:.6f}\")\n    \n    print(f\"Best inertia: {best_inertia:.6f}\")\n    \n    if best_centroids is not None:\n        # The centroids are unit vectors representing directions of A1 rows\n        # We need to recover the magnitude as well\n        # The magnitude is the norm of the gradient jump vector\n        # We already have the raw vectors, so let's also compute magnitude\n        \n        # For each centroid, find the average norm of vectors assigned to it\n        raw_vectors = vectors  # These are the actual gradient jumps, not normalized\n        raw_norms = np.linalg.norm(raw_vectors, axis=1)\n        \n        # Assign each raw vector to nearest centroid\n        assigned_norms = {i: [] for i in range(20)}\n        for idx, v in enumerate(raw_vectors):\n            v_norm = v / (np.linalg.norm(v) + 1e-10)\n            dists_pos = np.linalg.norm(best_centroids - v_norm.reshape(1, -1), axis=1)\n            dists_neg = np.linalg.norm(best_centroids + v_norm.reshape(1, -1), axis=1)\n            cluster = np.argmin(np.minimum(dists_pos, dists_neg))\n            assigned_norms[cluster].append(raw_norms[idx])\n        \n        # Build A1 matrix: each row is centroid * average_norm\n        A1_stolen = np.zeros((20, 10))\n        for i in range(20):\n            if len(assigned_norms[i]) > 0:\n                avg_norm = np.median(assigned_norms[i])\n                A1_stolen[i] = best_centroids[i] * avg_norm\n            else:\n                A1_stolen[i] = best_centroids[i]\n        \n        np.save('/app/stolen_A1.npy', A1_stolen)\n        print(\"Saved A1 to /app/stolen_A1.npy\")\n        print(f\"Shape: {A1_stolen.shape}\")\n    else:\n        print(\"Failed to extract A1\")\n\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    main()\nPYEOF\necho \"steal.py created\"\n",
